O, children, since I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, by its completion, its conclusion, and its explanations, it seems to me that I have fulfilled it for you with this treatise, which is a section of the manual operation, that is, surgery.
Because manual operation is largely lost in our region and time, almost all knowledge of it is lost; only a few small descriptions in the books of the ancients remain, which have led to errors and hesitation, so that the understanding of it, and the skill and art, have been lost.
And it seems to me that I will revive that [manual operation] through the organization of this treatise, in the way of exposition, explanation, and abbreviation; and so that it will come with the forms of cautery instruments and other tools of the craft, it is necessary to add a description and preparation of these.
But the reason why a skillful artisan with their hands is not found in our time is that the art of medicine is extensive, and that its practitioners must beforehand be practiced in the science of anatomy, which explains the structure of the limbs, and the forms of those, their connection and separation; and must have knowledge of the bones, nerves, and muscles, their number and arrangement; and of the pulsating and still veins, and the places of their emergence.
And for that reason, Hippocrates said that with one name [i.e., a general concept] it's a great deal, but in the practice [i.e., in the hands-on work] it's small, and especially in the art of the hand.
But we have already said this in the introduction to this book; because whoever is not familiar with what we have said about anatomy will certainly fall into an error by which men will die, as I have seen many of them; for some are trained in this science and abandon it without knowledge or experience.
For I saw a foolish and inexperienced physician attempt to lance a scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck, and opened some arteries in the neck so that a great deal of blood flowed until the woman died in his hands.
And I saw another physician attempt to remove a stone from a man who had suffered from it for a long time.  The stone was large, and he proceeded to remove it with a piece of the bladder, so that the man died on the third day.
And I, having already called myself to account, saw that because of the size of the stone and the patient's condition, I knew he would die.
And I saw another physician, who received payment from a duke in our land for surgery, and he was treating a black man who had a fractured thigh.  Through the physician's ignorance, he treated the fracture, applying bandages and splints with excessive pressure, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
And then he followed his desires, and then he bound it, and then he left it for a few days and commanded that we untie the ligament. And it remained like this until the thigh and the foot became abscessed, and led to destruction.
And I was called to him, and I proceeded to untie the ligament, and consequently, there was tranquility and a lessening of his pains.
However, since corruption was already established in the limb, I could not stop it, and the corruption continued in the limb until the patient perished.
And I saw another physician who opened a cancerous abscess, and it became ulcerated after a few days, until the evil of it was magnified by the patient's condition.
Since this condition is caused by black bile, it is not necessary to destroy it completely by any iron, but rather that the limb that suffers from its complete removal should be carefully considered.
And therefore, children, it is necessary for you that the operation be divided into two parts: one where the operation is associated with health, and the other where the operation holds danger in its most severe forms.
And I have already avoided this throughout this book in which the operation contains error and fear; therefore, it is necessary for you to guard against it and leave it aside, so that the pages do not find a way to speak and disgrace you.
Therefore, take your weapons with diligence and with God's protection, and your patients with happiness and firmness.
And use the best path, by God's grace, aiming for health and praiseworthy success, and abandon those terrible illnesses with difficult cures, and remove from your armour anything that makes you afraid, so that your faith and your name might not fail you: for greater glory remains for you, and higher in the world and behind your holiness.
Already has Gualia said in some of her teachings: Do not treat a bad illness, so that you are not called bad doctors.
And I have now divided this book into three chapters.
Begins the division of the book, and first of the first part. The first chapter, ordered from head to foot, describes the forms of instruments and the tools for cauteries, and what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, on cutting, piercing, cupping, poultices, the extraction of arrows and similar things, is a complete and ordered chapter concerning the forms of instruments.
The third chapter, on restoration and dislocation, and the treatment of twisting and similar things; a chapter ordered from head to foot, and concerning the forms of instruments.
It is necessary for me to explain the benefits and harms of this cautery, and in what constitution it is forbidden.
Therefore I say that the discourse on the benefits and harms of cautery is long and verbose, subtle in its science, and a hidden secret; and many learned people have already spoken of it, and disagreed about it, but a little of their discourse will suffice me, fearing to prolong it.
And therefore I say that cautery benefits all constitutions universally, whether with matter or without matter, except for two constitutions, which are hot constitutions without matter.
In the hot and dry constitution with matter, there is disagreement; for some say that cautery is beneficial for that, and others say the opposite, that cautery is not suitable for an illness that is characterized by heat and dryness, because the nature of fire is heat and dryness, and it is not appropriate for a hot and dry illness to be cured with something that is also hot and dry.
And those who say the opposite argue that cautery is beneficial in every hot and dry illness affecting the body, because when you compare the body and its humours to the constitution of fire, you find the body to be cold.
And I say, concerning this matter, that experience has revealed this to me on several occasions.
However, it is not appropriate for someone to comment on this who has not already been practiced and skilled in the chapter on cautery through prior exercise, and who has not understood the diversity of human constitutions, the nature of diseases in themselves, their causes, their symptoms, and the appropriate timeframe for treating them.
But in other constitutions, there is no need for concern, and especially in cold and moist illnesses, for all physicians have agreed on these, and there is no disagreement on the benefit of cautery in such cases.
And know, children, that the secret of healing through cautery with fire, and its efficacy, differs from cautery with medicinal burning agents, because fire is simple, its action only affects the part cauterized, and does not harm other parts connected to it, except with minor harm.
But the action of medicinal burning agents reaches those parts of the body that are distant from the application, and easily causes difficult-to-heal illnesses and severe harm in the affected part.
However, fire, due to its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, but rather it's superfluous.  And this is already known to us through experimentation and long study of the art of understanding the truth of causes; and because of this, I am excused from a long discourse.  If it were not that it is not written in my book on this subject, and that the secrets related to fire, its effect on the body, and the expulsion of ailments by means of fire, are hidden from you, a philosophical demonstration would be appropriate for your understanding.
And know, children, that they disagree about the time when cautery is most appropriate, and they suggest the best time is spring.
And I say that cautery is appropriate at any time, because the harm caused by an inappropriate time is outweighed by the benefit of what is removed with cautery, especially if the cautery is performed for severe and urgent pains or ailments that cannot tolerate delay because the feared harm (the disease) is greater than the minor damage that time might cause.
And this is not in your understanding, or children, this is only believed by the ignorant populace and foolish physicians, that is to say, that the disease cured by cautery is not always beneficial, and they ignore the consequences.
And the reason is not at all as they suppose, for cautery is not just any medicine that alters the constitution and dries out the humors that are the cause of the pain.
But nevertheless, cautery is superior to other medicine because of its power and efficacy, and the greatness of its effect.
And it is possible that the illness may return at some time, depending on the patient's constitution, the location of the illness, the patient's strength, and the accumulation of superfluous humors in the body, as well as what has been acquired through their diet and similar causes.  However, if the illness for which cautery is administered is a localized ailment with only a small amount of superfluous humors and moisture, such as toothache and similar conditions, it is possible that the pain will not return, but this is in small cases.
And it is a common saying that cautery is the last resort in medicine, and this is a true statement, not in the way they understand it, for they believe there is no cure that benefits more than cautery.
And the reason is the opposite of that; the idea that cautery is the last resort in medicine is only true when, in some illnesses, we have exhausted other methods of treatment and those remedies have not helped, and then at the end of the process, cautery is applied and proves useful. And therefore, the statement that cautery is the last resort in medicine is not true according to the understanding of the common people and many foolish doctors.
And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they said this only because of the nobility and superior nature of gold's substance.
And they said that the place of cautery does not do harm, though this is not entirely true, for I have tested this and found that it only does so in certain bodies and not others, and cautery with gold is good and better than with iron, as they said; however, when you perform cautery with gold, it is not immediately evident, because it is heated according to the amount you desire by the density of the gold, and because it is prepared to receive cold; and if you apply heat, the gold melts in the fire, and in the fire certain flakes fall, so that the craftsman is harmed by the work.
Therefore, cautery with iron is done more easily and more appropriately for the correctness of the operation.
And I have organized this chapter on cautery according to topics, and I have arranged them from head to feet, so that the seeker can find what they need.
The first chapter.
This cauterization addresses the dampness and cold affecting the brain, which has two main causes:  an excess of rheumatic fluid (called catarrh), flowing from the head to the eye and ear areas;  excessive sleep; toothache; and pain in the throat.  More generally, it treats all illnesses stemming from cold, including paralysis, stroke, and similar conditions.
The method for this cauterization is as follows: first, instruct the patient to take laxative medicine to clear the head for three or four nights, depending on the patient's strength, age, and usual response.
Then, tell him to shave his head, and afterwards, place him on a smooth bench with your hands supporting his feet.
And then place the blade of your palm (or the blade of the instrument) near the bridge of his nose, between his eyes. However, once your middle finger has reached the place, mark that spot with a probe, and then apply the olive-oil cautery, the process for which is as follows:
Then place it (the cautery) on the spot marked by the probe,  so that it descends, gradually pressing your hand down, and you rotate it.
Then gently lift your hand and observe the area. If you see a noticeable amount of bone exposed, about the size of a grain of millet, then elevate your hand, and if not, return your hand with the iron, another one from the set, if it's cooled down, until the bone is visible as I told you.
Then take a small amount of salt and dissolve it over the area and leave it for three days.
Then apply a cloth soaked in broth and leave it on until the scab from the burn is destroyed. And then treat the area with tetrafarmacon ointment until it is healed.
And if the wound remains open, the better you move the arm, because it is better and more helpful.
And some of them say that the bone should be cauterized down to the bone, and the cautery should be held until some part of the bone's marrow is burned.
And then whatever is burned off the bone should be scraped off, and then it should be treated.
And others say that with the cautery they should proceed to the back, until it firmly presses on the bone, so that the bone gives way.  This is the method of a small cauterization. And they believe that vapors from the head escape from that area.
And the wound should be kept open for a long time, and then treated until it is healed.
However, I have not seen these two types of cauterization in all cases, but in some people according to a fearful approach; and in my opinion, it is better, when possible, with healing, for the head is weakened by the disruption of its continuity, just as we have seen in other limbs, and especially when the patient's head is of a weak constitution.
And the first type of cauterization is safer and better in my opinion; and by using it and with that procedure, healing occurs.
Second Chapter.
Of the cauterization of the head.
When chronic and prolonged pain affects the entire head in a prolonged illness, and treatments like leeches, cups, head purges, plasters, poultices, baths, lotions, and similar remedies have been used, and especially if it has already been cauterized with a cauterization method that we have described and no benefit comes from those things, then consider that if the patient's head has a strong constitution, and it is not frail and is subjected to considerable cold, then cauterize with another cauterization technique beneath the first one a little bit. And then cauterize that area over the patient's forehead with a cauterizing instrument until the pain is relieved. Cut open the pain and expose the bone to the extent we described, and cauterize that area with a cautery on the back of the head, in the location called the *vas* (vein) – which is the area where a cupping vessel is placed. And ease your hand in doing this, and do not expose the bone, for the patient will experience very severe pain, different from the pain caused by other cauteries of the head.
And I would advise this cautery in this place, because the cautery used for cauterizing the temples and occiput should be a more delicate cautery than that used to cauterize the middle of the head; and this is the method for it.
Third Chapter.
Of the cauterization of non-chronic migraines.
When a constant or spreading pain occurs in the head, or extends to the eye, the head should be cleared with medicaments, and the other treatment, which I have described in the discussions of illnesses, should be administered; and if all of this is ineffective, then cauterization in that area is done in two ways: either with a sharp, burning medicine, or with iron.
But cauterization with a burning medicine is that you take a clove of garlic, and squeeze it and incise the extremities of it at both ends. And then you cut the area of pain in the temple with a sharp lancet until a space is made beneath the skin, until it is hidden.
Then press on it with a bandage to constrict it, and leave it for three hours; and then remove it and take away the garlic, and let the wound be for two or three days, and then apply cotton soaked in butter until the area heals.
And then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, do this with some burning medicines, which I have written about in the second treatise on burning medicines.
But cauterization with iron, according to this method:  heat the cautery iron, of which this is the form:
and it is called a "claus clavilhs," for its head is like the shape of a nail, in which there is some curvature, and in the middle of it is a small eminence.
Then place it on the painful area, and hold your hand — so the underlying skin isn't burned — and rotate the iron slowly with speed.
And if the amount burned by the sharpness of the cautery is about half, then lift your hand so the underlying artery isn't burned, to prevent blood flow.
Then soak cotton in salt water and place it on the area, and leave it for three days; then place cotton soaked in butter, and then treat with ointment until healed.
And if you wish, cauterize with the sharp edge of a knife as a cautery, and be careful not to cut an artery in this particular, somewhat unusual, procedure.
Fourth Chapter.
On the cauterization of an old migraine.
When you treat a migraine using what we have described in the previous treatment and what we have discussed in the divisions of illnesses, and the treatment proves ineffective, and sometimes the ailment resists what we have described regarding the initial cauterization with medicine or cauterization with fire, then you must heat the knife cautery until it is white-hot, then draw a line on the area of pain, a length equal to half a finger or thereabouts; press your hand down once, and press firmly until you cut into the artery and penetrate down to the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to be careful of the continuation of the jawbone, which is strained by chewing, and that the ligaments and nerves that control it are not overly tense and that a spasm does not result.
And if it is about the care and caution of the blood flow from the cut artery, for fear exists in its cutting, and even more so for him who does not understand what he does and is not studious and skilled; and he abandons the operation at the beginning.
And I will bring a reminder of the treatment for accidental blood flow from an artery according to its method, in its place in this book.
And if you see that this ailment is not relieved by this cautery and you see the patient's condition as tolerable, cauterize the middle of the head as we have described, and treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cautery that we have described in the chapter on the constriction of arteries with a cautery having two blades; this is a better and more beneficial cauterization.
Chapter 5.
Of the cauterization of earaches.
When pain in the ear is caused by cold and is treated with laxative remedies and the other treatments mentioned in the previous section, and the pain persists, then apply the cautery, specifically the one called the *puncta* (pointed cautery).  Its form is this:
And then, apply the heated point [of the cautery] around the ear, moving it in a circular motion, or in a circuit around affected areas if the pain is localized. Move the cautery from the base of the ear slowly, after marking the area with a probe.
And if the cautery is used with ten points throughout the ear, then treat the affected areas until they heal.
Chapter 6.
On the cauterization of the tumour.
A tumour that is cured with cauterization is only of the types that arise from phlegm, as we have stated in the divisions of illnesses.
Avoid cauterization of the type that comes from drying or spasm of the nerve.
When you treat that type of tumor with herbs, purging, and other remedies, and your treatment does not work, then you should cauterize the patient with three cauteries: the first at the root of the ear, the second a little below the temple, and the third at the juncture of the two lips.
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the diseased area, for softening only comes to the side that appears healthy.
And the method of cauterization is to cauterize the area directly at the end of the ear, slightly above the corner of the head, and another one on the temple, the length of which should be equal to the length of the index finger, and hold the cautery there until the quantity of the inflamed portion of the condition has been burned away by half.
And this is the form of the cauterization, and it is a type of surgical procedure, the form of which is set forth below. However, it is more subtle than that described; and it is necessary to cut away a little of the superfluous thickness there.
And then treat the area with what has been previously described until it is healed.
Chapter 7.
Of cauterization for old apoplexy.
When apoplexy is old and you have treated it with what we have said, and your treatment is not effective, and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize with four cauteries: on all the temples of their head; and with a cautery on the middle of the head, as we have said; and with a cautery on the neck. And the manner of cauterization is done according to what has been previously stated.
And it has already been cauterized on the mouth of the stomach; and further back; and then it should be treated with the following procedures.
Chapter 8.
Of cauterization of oblivion caused by flame.
There should be given to the sick person at the beginning large jars and pills that purify the brain.
And then shave the entire head of the patient and apply a plaster of centaury, as described in the treatise on plasters, to the patient's temples.
And apply that several times, for that is a method of cauterization. And do this according to the same order which I have already mentioned.
And so if by that treatment he is cured, well and good; but if not, then apply three cauteries to the back part of his head, which descend from the most superior part of the head down to the part of the neck below. And place the thickness of the finger between each cautery, and then treat the cautery with what has been previously described.
But if you wish to increase the application, and the patient can tolerate it, then apply a cautery in the middle location; and if you wish a greater application, then cauterize it over the two horns.
Then treat it until it is healed; and let the cautery be oily according to the previously given method.
Chapter 9.
Of the cauterization of paralysis and the softening of the whole body.
You should proceed with cleaning the head with herbs and as we have said; and then shave the patient's head, and then cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery on all the horns of the head, and with a cautery on the back part of it, and with three cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck.
And if in the illness of softening of the body, the patient and the illness are severe, then cauterize it with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and subsequently with a cautery until it is softened from the spinal cord, and remove your hand. And then treat it until it is healed, and this should be an olive cautery.
Chapter 10.
On the cauterization of epilepsy.
The epileptic is not cauterized unless the epilepsy is due to phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary to treat the brain from the beginning with herbs and other treatments that we have discussed in the section when the patient is severe and able to tolerate the impact of medicines.
And if it is a child who cannot tolerate the medicines, then administer remedies and chewing agents that treat the brain, previously for many days, with a beneficial diet.
Then shave the patient's head, and then cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, following the previous method, and with another cautery on the back of their head, and cauterize on each temple of their head. And if the illness is severe and able to tolerate it, then cauterize it with the cauteries I have mentioned, having simultaneously paralysis and softening of the body, on the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back.
Let the cautery be olive-oil-based, as was previously described.
But if the patient is a child, then place a delicate cautery, according to this method.
Chapter 11.
Concerning the cauterization of melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize that with the cauteries that we have described in the section on paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is a superfluity inclining towards melancholy, and the patient's body is humid, then give him to drink that which purifies his brain, according to what has been previously stated in the division.
And then shave the patient's head, and then apply a properly made plaster to it around the circumference, and then place that in the middle of the head.
And the patient should be seated upright, and supported on all sides.
And then apply liniment; and a boiled sheep's wool is even more worthy. And heat that over the fire with a moderate heating, which the said patient can tolerate when it is applied to him. And then apply that to the middle of his head in a circular motion, and leave it until it has cooled.
And do this with the patient once a week, with the other remedies for him until he is healed; or, if you wish, cauterize the area making small punctures according to his tolerance, but keep your hand with a properly arranged cautery. This is a type of cautery which moistens the brain evenly.
And then apply this cloth soaked in boiled or warmed wine.
Chapter 12.
Concerning the cauterization of descending water in the eye.
When you have observed the beginning of water in the eye according to the signs described in the previous section, then begin giving the patient a drink that will modify the condition of his head and protect him from all moisture.
And have him sweat in a bath for several days.
Then command him to shave his head, and cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of his head; and then cauterize with two cauteries on both temples if the water affliction is in both eyes, or on one temple if the affliction is in one eye.
Cauterize all the veins and arteries under the temple; and let the cauteries be of that length in the breadth of the temples.
And be careful of blood flow when cauterizing; and if you see blood flowing from him, stop it with any medicine possible to you.
And I will come with skill in the extraction of arteries and with the excision of them and precaution against blood flow.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck between the two bones with two cauteries directly applied.
Chapter 13.
Of the cauterization of old sores.
When sores on the face are old, persistent, and through the veins and arteries visible on the surface of the head, and it is clear that this is due to cold phlegmatic superfluities, then cauterize this with the cautery we described in the chapter beginning with hot water on the sores, and with a cautery in the middle of the head and with two cauteries on the neck below the temples, and with two cauteries on the neck below the two bones. And if further treatment is needed, then cauterize that along the entire edge of the sore on the eyebrow's extremity with a small cautery.
Chapter 14.
Of cauterization of a foul odor from the nose.
When you treat it with what we've discussed in the division and your treatment is ineffective, then you prepare and give the patient poppy seeds to drink for three nights; and then wash his/her head, and cauterize it with a milder cautery and an olive cautery. And then cauterize it with a clove cautery, using two cauteries on the two eyebrows below the hair, a small one.
And be careful of the spark so you don't set it on fire.
And this is the form of the clove cautery.
Chapter 15.
Of cautery for softening the eyelids of the eyes.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by illness or moisture, then cauterize that eyelid with a cautery using this lunar cautery; and this is its form:
And if you [do so], cauterize the area above the two eyebrows slightly with two cauteries, in all directions, and they should be elongated from the temples. And the length of each cautery should be according to the amount of eyebrow.
And do not press your hand with the cautery too hard, but according to the amount needed to adhere the third part of the eyelid.
Chapter 16.
Concerning cauterization of the eyelid when the lashes have grown inward and are irritating the eye.
When the eyelashes of the eye have turned inward, irritating the eye, cauterization in such cases is done in two ways: either with a burning iron or with a burning medicine.
If with a cautery using fire, first instruct the patient to remove their eyelashes, as if one would pluck them, until they are elongated and plucked out; and if you cauterize just beneath their roots, then bind their eyes with a bandage so that they are not irritated until the eyelashes have grown back.
Then, when they have grown back and been plucked out, place the patient's head on your lap, and carefully apply a cautery to the eyelid(s) using a cautery tool shaped like a myrtle leaf, starting the mark near the lashes.
Then place cotton soaked in egg white or a pilli mixture over the eye.
And then apply the cautery, which has this shape.
And then cauterize the marked area, little by little, many times, until the surface of the skin, which is like a myrtle leaf, is completely charred.
A sign of successful treatment is that you see the eyelid drawn in and the eyelashes raised towards the puncture in the eye.
And then raise your hand and leave it for three days, and then place cotton with lint over it until the scab is removed. And then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
But if any cause returns to the roots of the hair, and the eyelid is softened, then do the cauterization again, just as you did at first.
But if the hairs are under the eyelid, then cauterize them until they are raised to their natural place and are embedded, and the hairs no longer prick the eye.
But the cautery with burning medicine is that you command the patient to leave the hairs until they are elongated and embedded, and then a leaf-shaped piece of cloth should be made, in the form of a myrtle leaf.
And then take known herbs and living ash, or similar things, and thoroughly mix those substances quickly, so that it does not become cold; and then spread this mixture onto the cloth shaped like a myrtle leaf, and place that over the one or both eyes; and place a cloth soaked in egg white underneath the eye, and the patient's head should be in your care.
And place your finger on the medicine and press it slightly, but don't remove it until the patient feels the medicine's burning sensation, because the burning is like a fire.
And therefore, when the patient feels the burning sensation, remove the medicine and wash it away with your finger; then, when the burning subsides, remove the medicine and wash the eye with water; then observe whether the eyelid has already risen, as if cleansed of the constriction by fire or incision, for then it is good; and if not, return to applying the medicine to the area where the medicine wasn't applied, and do not give up until your treatment is embedded and the eye is healed.
And then place a cloth over it until the burn is healed, and then treat it with a definitive ointment or another remedy until it is cured.
It is necessary for you, during your treatment, to carefully guard against anything from the medicine falling into the eye, and if the eyelid softens after a few days and some substance from the eyelashes gets into the eye, then repeat your application of medicine to the softened area of the eyelid, just as you did at the beginning, and continue this until it is healed.
And this is the method of treating a wound with myrrh.
And know that human wounds vary in size and severity, and therefore your treatment is performed accordingly.
And the path to recovery will not be hidden from him who studies this art.
Chapter 17.
Concerning the cauterization of fistulas in the tear duct of a wound.
When you treat a fistula as described in the classifications of diseases, and your treatment does not improve, you must cauterize it in this manner: instruct the patient to rest their head on your lap, and have an assistant hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it is neither moved nor shaken by their head.
And then apply a piece of cotton dipped in egg white or marshmallow pulp over the wound.
And then apply the cautery, which has this shape:
which is concave, like the shape of a reed or a hawk's wing, on one end where the cautery is made.
And if desired, it should be penetrating to the other end. And if you want, it should be shaped like a probe.
But nevertheless, the concave one is better for your work.
And then press the fistula if it is open, and through it drain and dry that [infected area]. And if it is not open, then open it and extract the pus from it.
And then place the cautery, which is well ignited, on it, and hold it with your hand a little away from the cautery's point, towards the nose area, so that your hand does not stray or the patient is disturbed, and then place the cautery on the inflamed area and cauterize it.
And therefore, if at the beginning of your cauterization you penetrate to the bone, it is good; and if not, then repeat the cauterization once or twice, if necessary; and leave it like that for three days, and then apply cotton with oil and surround it with a drying ointment until it is healed.
But if more than ten days have passed and it is not healed, then apply a sharp, corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed and is clean as is appropriate in your chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some earlier practitioners used:  Apply a cautery to the fistula and cauterize it, then place a thin, shaped piece of melted lead into the fissure.  Hold it in place with your hand, securely, to avoid moving the patient, so the melted lead does not reach the sore.  Cover the patient's skin over the fistula with a bandage dipped in egg white or water, because melted lead adheres to the fistula area and heals it with marvelous recovery.
And if the fistula is healed with the cauterization and treatment we have described, that is good; but if not, then it is necessary to administer a nasal passage and reduce the fistula to the body of the nose, returning it to its proper place.
Chapter 18.
Concerning the cauterization of a fissure in the pot (or perhaps, a fissure in the body).
Often, fissures occur in the lips, and more so in the lips of children.
Therefore, if you treat those fissures using the methods we have described in the divisions and your treatment is not successful, then heat a small, knife-like cautery according to this form shown below:

Of cauterization of fistulas in the mouth.

Chapter 20.
Of cauterization of the teeth and softening of the gums.

Keep your hand there for a short time so the patient feels the heat of the fire reaching the root of the tooth.
And then remove your hand, and then repeat the cauterization several times as desired.
And then the patient should fill their mouth with salt water and hold it for an hour, and then spit it out, for the decayed tooth is sealed, the softened gums are strengthened, and the corrupt moisture is dried.
Chapter 21.
Concerning the cauterization of toothache.

Cauterization with a bladder is done by taking a cow's bladder, boiling it in an iron container, then taking a piece of cloth and wrapping it around the tip of the probe, dipping that wrapped cloth into the boiled bladder, and quickly placing it on the aching tooth until it cools down.
And then repeat this several times until the effect of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, dip wool or cloth in the aforementioned bladder, place that on the aching tooth, and place the heated iron on top of it until the iron reaches the bottom of the tooth cavity.
However, cauterization with fire is done by holding a needle or iron, ensuring its thickness is appropriate so that the heat does not reach the patient's mouth.
Then heat the cautery, whatever shape it may be, and place it on the tooth, holding it until the cautery cools; repeat this several times until the pain subsides, either that day or the next.
And it is necessary that, during the application of the cautery, the patient fill his/her mouth with a good potion and hold it for an hour, and then spit it out; and this is the method of cauterization.

Chapter 28.
Of the perforation of a liver abscess with cautery.

Of the cauterization of pleurisy.

Then immerse it in oil and heat it in the fire, and then cauterize the area between the continuation of the collarbone and the neck with a cautery.  Use two smaller cauteries slightly angled downward toward the area below the beard, and two more cauteries angled slightly downward between the fifth and sixth ribs, behind the area. Use a cautery on the area between the shoulder blades, and two more cauteries on the sides of the back, below the cautery between the shoulder blades.

And there is another way to cauterize, which is to ignite the cautery using two incisions, as described in the chapter on muscle dislocations, and lift the ribcage on the side of the spleen where the patient's left side lies.

And if you wish, cauterize with a cautery having three incisions.
And now you treat the cautery, since it has stopped emitting pus after several days, for this is more important than the other preceding actions in the cure.

Of the cauterization of dropsy.
Cautery is not applied to dropsy but to elephantiasis properly.

And the depth of the cautery should be proportional to the severity of the condition.
And leave the cautery open so that it discharges pus for a long time.

The shape of the cautery used to cauterize the belly should be wedge-shaped, following the shape of the previous one; and the shape of the cautery used to cauterize the back should be olive-shaped, following the previous one's shape.

Chapter 36.
Of the cauterization of fistulas that have formed naturally in various parts of the body.

And be careful not to burn any nerves or veins; or if the fistula goes towards the bladder or towards the intestines, then be careful about those areas; and do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshy area and you believe it is not penetrating.
Then treat the area until it is healed.
And if the area is sealed, and the matter has been removed from it, and it remains like that for a long time, then know that it is completely healed.
And if the matter is not removed from it, then know that it is penetrating or in the proximity of a diseased part, or that it comes from those causes which will return to the area.

Albucasis says:  O, children, we have used little of this type of cautery because of the fear of its appearance, and because few have been found who look upon it with approval.
But of the good cauteries, to those who endure them, and find with it the place of their affliction.

Then raise your hand with the instrument and wipe away the hot water from the entire affected area with fresh water.
Then leave it for three days and apply a bandage until the blackness of the burn remains, and leave it for several days, and the area will heal; this is the final treatment.
And then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
And if the pain extends to the thigh or leg, make a poultice for the affected area that contains water, as was done for the affected area of the foot.
And this is the method of applying hot water, and I have already written about it in my treatise on the rectification of medicine. Take a portion of potash and quicklime, each one part, and crush them. Place them in a new pot, the bottom of which has a small hole,  corresponding to the size of the wound.
And place another, lined pot beneath the bottom of the first pot.  Pour fresh, sweet water over the potash and quicklime in the top pot, gradually, a little at a time.  Then, after you have thoroughly mixed them by hand, let the excess, now caustic, water drain down into the lower lined pot.
Then collect all that water and pour it over fresh quicklime and potash, for it will now be highly caustic.  This is used in many medical procedures and for cauterizing other parts of the body, as it acts as a form of fire.
And some of the medicines used for cauterization include:  teazizic, honey, and quicklime with some kind of spice, mixed together in this way.

He says that a simple bath and this treatment is enough.

And then place him in a bath, and when his body is thoroughly warmed, lay him on the ground, for the pain will cease and he will be cured.

Then take a dry goat's horn, and heat it over fire until it is charred; and then place it on the wool and leave it there until it has spread out. And repeat this, and do not stop doing this until the sensation of the biting [pain] reaches the chest and the pain subsides.
And this method of cautery is called the cautery of goats (or "goat's horn cautery").
